#PROJECT
PR:PROJECT_TITLE                 	Evidence that COG0325 proteins are involved in Pyridoxal 5'-phosphate (PLP)
PR:PROJECT_TITLE                 	homeostasis
PR:PROJECT_SUMMARY               	Pyridoxal 5'-phosphate (PLP) is an essential cofactor for nearly 60 Escherichia
PR:PROJECT_SUMMARY               	coli enzymes but is a highly reactive molecule that is toxic in its free form.
PR:PROJECT_SUMMARY               	How PLP levels are regulated and how PLP is delivered to target enzymes are
PR:PROJECT_SUMMARY               	still open questions. The COG0325 protein family belongs to the fold-type III
PR:PROJECT_SUMMARY               	class of PLP enzymes and binds PLP but has no known biochemical activity
PR:PROJECT_SUMMARY               	although it occurs in all kingdoms of life. Various pleiotropic phenotypes of
PR:PROJECT_SUMMARY               	the E. coli COG0325 (yggS) mutant have been reported, some of which were
PR:PROJECT_SUMMARY               	reproduced and extended in this study. Comparative genomic, genetic and
PR:PROJECT_SUMMARY               	metabolic analyses suggest that these phenotypes reflect an imbalance in PLP
PR:PROJECT_SUMMARY               	homeostasis. The E. coli yggS mutant accumulates the PLP precursor pyridoxine
PR:PROJECT_SUMMARY               	5'-phosphate (PNP) and is sensitive to an excess of pyridoxine but not of
PR:PROJECT_SUMMARY               	pyridoxal. The pyridoxine toxicity phenotype is complemented by the expression
PR:PROJECT_SUMMARY               	of eukaryotic yggS orthologs. It is also suppressed by the presence of amino
PR:PROJECT_SUMMARY               	acids, specifically isoleucine, threonine and leucine, suggesting the
PR:PROJECT_SUMMARY               	PLP-dependent enzyme transaminase B (IlvE) is affected. These genetic results
PR:PROJECT_SUMMARY               	lay a foundation for future biochemical studies of the role of COG0325 proteins
PR:PROJECT_SUMMARY               	in PLP homeostasis.
PR:INSTITUTE                     	University of Florida
PR:DEPARTMENT                    	Microbiology and Cell Science
PR:LAST_NAME                     	de Crecy-Lagard
PR:FIRST_NAME                    	Valerie
PR:ADDRESS                       	Gainesville, FL 32611
PR:EMAIL                         	vcrecy@ufl.edu
PR:PHONE                         	352-392-9416
#STUDY
ST:STUDY_TITLE                   	Evidence that COG0325 proteins are involved in PLP homeostasis
ST:STUDY_SUMMARY                 	Pyridoxal 5'-phosphate (PLP) is an essential cofactor for nearly 60 Escherichia

ST:STUDY_SUMMARY                 	How PLP levels are regulated and how PLP is delivered to target enzymes are
ST:STUDY_SUMMARY                 	still open questions. The COG0325 protein family belongs to the fold-type III
ST:STUDY_SUMMARY                 	class of PLP enzymes and binds PLP but has no known biochemical activity
ST:STUDY_SUMMARY                 	although it occurs in all kingdoms of life. Various pleiotropic phenotypes of
ST:STUDY_SUMMARY                 	the E. coli COG0325 (yggS) mutant have been reported, some of which were
ST:STUDY_SUMMARY                 	reproduced and extended in this study. Comparative genomic, genetic and
ST:STUDY_SUMMARY                 	metabolic analyses suggest that these phenotypes reflect an imbalance in PLP
ST:STUDY_SUMMARY                 	homeostasis. The E. coli yggS mutant accumulates the PLP precursor pyridoxine
ST:STUDY_SUMMARY                 	5'-phosphate (PNP) and is sensitive to an excess of pyridoxine but not of
ST:STUDY_SUMMARY                 	pyridoxal. The pyridoxine toxicity phenotype is complemented by the expression
ST:STUDY_SUMMARY                 	of eukaryotic yggS orthologs. It is also suppressed by the presence of amino
ST:STUDY_SUMMARY                 	acids, specifically isoleucine, threonine and leucine, suggesting the
ST:STUDY_SUMMARY                 	PLP-dependent enzyme transaminase B (IlvE) is affected. These genetic results
ST:STUDY_SUMMARY                 	lay a foundation for future biochemical studies of the role of COG0325 proteins
ST:STUDY_SUMMARY                 	in PLP homeostasis.

ST:STUDY_COMMENTS                	LB stands for Luria Bertani medium. MG stands for minimal growth For strains
ST:STUDY_COMMENTS                	grown on MG OD 0.5 is the mid log growth phase and OD 1.0 is the late log growth
ST:STUDY_COMMENTS                	phase For strains grown on LB OD 1 is the mid log growth phase and OD 2.0 is the
ST:STUDY_COMMENTS                	late log growth phase

#COLLECTION
CO:COLLECTION_SUMMARY            	Cells were grown overnight in M9 glucose 0.2% (w/v) supplemented with 1 mM
CO:COLLECTION_SUMMARY            	glycine at 37 °C, and then were diluted to an OD of 0.03 in M9 glucose 0.2%
CO:COLLECTION_SUMMARY            	(w/v) supplemented with 1 mM glycine. Mid-log (OD600=0.5) or late-log (OD600=1)
CO:COLLECTION_SUMMARY            	samples were centrifuged for 20 s at 13,500 g and stored at -80 °C.
CO:SAMPLE_TYPE                   	Cell
#TREATMENT
TR:TREATMENT_SUMMARY             	Bacteria were grown on Luria Bertani (LB) medium (BD Diagnostics Systems) at
TR:TREATMENT_SUMMARY             	37°C or on M9 minimal medium supplemented with 0.2 % (w/v) glucose and 1 mM
TR:TREATMENT_SUMMARY             	glycine
#SAMPLEPREP
SP:SAMPLEPREP_SUMMARY            	B6 species [PLP, PNP, pyridoxamine 5'-phosphate (PMP), PL, PN and PM] were
SP:SAMPLEPREP_SUMMARY            	extracted from WT and ΔyggS pellets (1.0 ml culture of OD60051.0) in 0.9 ml 5 %
SP:SAMPLEPREP_SUMMARY            	(w/v) metaphosphoric acid and 0.1 ml internal standard 4-deoxypyridoxine (73
SP:SAMPLEPREP_SUMMARY            	nmol/ml in 5 % metaphosphoric acid). The suspension was vortexed and sonicated.
SP:SAMPLEPREP_SUMMARY            	After centrifugation at 10 000 g for 15 min, the supernatant was filtered and a
SP:SAMPLEPREP_SUMMARY            	50 ml sample was taken for HPLC analysis using fluorescence detection
SP:SAMPLEPREP_SUMMARY            	(excitation 328 nm, emission 393 nm).
